78. /** Feed a background worker result into the orchestrator as a new turn. */
79. export function feedBackgroundResult(workerName: string, result: string): void {
80.   const worker = workers.get(workerName);
81.   const channel = worker?.originChannel;
82.   const prompt = `[Background task completed] Worker '${workerName}' finished:\n\n${result}`;
83.   sendToOrchestrator(
84.     prompt,
85.     { type: "background" },
86.     (_text, done) => {
87.       if (done && proactiveNotifyFn) {
88.         proactiveNotifyFn(_text, channel);
89.       }
90.     }
91.   );
92. }

94. function sleep(ms: number): Promise<void> {
95.   return new Promise((resolve) => setTimeout(resolve, ms));
96. }

98. /** Ensure the SDK client is connected, resetting if necessary. Coalesces concurrent resets. */
99. let resetPromise: Promise<CopilotClient> | undefined;
100. async function ensureClient(): Promise<CopilotClient> {
101.   if (copilotClient && copilotClient.getState() === "connected") {
102.     return copilotClient;
103.   }
104.   if (!resetPromise) {
105.     console.log(`[max] Client not connected (state: ${copilotClient?.getState() ?? "null"}), resetting…`);
106.     resetPromise = resetClient().then((c) => {
107.       console.log(`[max] Client reset successful, state: ${c.getState()}`);
108.       copilotClient = c;
109.       return c;
110.     }).finally(() => { resetPromise = undefined; });
111.   }
112.   return resetPromise;
113. }
114. 
115. /** Start periodic health check that proactively reconnects the client. */
116. function startHealthCheck(): void {
117.   if (healthCheckTimer) return;
118.   healthCheckTimer = setInterval(async () => {
119.     if (!copilotClient) return;
120.     try {
121.       const state = copilotClient.getState();
122.       if (state !== "connected") {
123.         console.log(`[max] Health check: client state is '${state}', resetting…`);
124.         await ensureClient();
125.         // Session may need recovery after client reset
126.         orchestratorSession = undefined;
127.       }
128.     } catch (err) {
129.       console.error(`[max] Health check error:`, err instanceof Error ? err.message : err);
130.     }
131.   }, HEALTH_CHECK_INTERVAL_MS);
132. }
133. 
134. /** Create or resume the persistent orchestrator session. */
135. async function ensureOrchestratorSession(): Promise<CopilotSession> {
136.   if (orchestratorSession) return orchestratorSession;
137.   // Coalesce concurrent callers — wait for an in-flight creation
138.   if (sessionCreatePromise) return sessionCreatePromise;
139. 
140.   sessionCreatePromise = createOrResumeSession();
141.   try {
142.     const session = await sessionCreatePromise;
143.     orchestratorSession = session;
144.     return session;
145.   } finally {
146.     sessionCreatePromise = undefined;
147.   }
148. }
149. 
150. /** Internal: actually create or resume a session (not concurrency-safe — use ensureOrchestratorSession). */
151. async function createOrResumeSession(): Promise<CopilotSession> {
152.   const client = await ensureClient();
153.   const { tools, mcpServers, skillDirectories } = getSessionConfig();
154.   const memorySummary = getMemorySummary();
155. 
156.   const infiniteSessions = {
157.     enabled: true,
158.     backgroundCompactionThreshold: 0.80,
159.     bufferExhaustionThreshold: 0.95,
160.   };
161. 
162.   // Try to resume a previous session
163.   const savedSessionId = getState(ORCHESTRATOR_SESSION_KEY);
164.   if (savedSessionId) {
165.     try {
166.       console.log(`[max] Resuming orchestrator session ${savedSessionId.slice(0, 8)}…`);
167.       const session = await client.resumeSession(savedSessionId, {
168.         model: config.copilotModel,
169.         configDir: SESSIONS_DIR,
170.         streaming: true,
171.         systemMessage: {
172.           content: getOrchestratorSystemMessage(memorySummary || undefined, { selfEditEnabled: config.selfEditEnabled }),
173.         },
174.         tools,
175.         mcpServers,
176.         skillDirectories,
177.         onPermissionRequest: approveAll,
178.         infiniteSessions,
179.       });
180.       console.log(`[max] Resumed orchestrator session successfully`);
181.       return session;
182.     } catch (err) {
183.       console.log(`[max] Could not resume session: ${err instanceof Error ? err.message : err}. Creating new.`);
184.       deleteState(ORCHESTRATOR_SESSION_KEY);
185.     }
186.   }
187. 
188.   // Create a fresh session
189.   console.log(`[max] Creating new persistent orchestrator session`);
190.   const session = await client.createSession({
191.     model: config.copilotModel,
192.     configDir: SESSIONS_DIR,
193.     streaming: true,
194.     systemMessage: {
195.       content: getOrchestratorSystemMessage(memorySummary || undefined, { selfEditEnabled: config.selfEditEnabled }),
196.     },
197.     tools,
198.     mcpServers,
199.     skillDirectories,
200.     onPermissionRequest: approveAll,
201.     infiniteSessions,
202.   });
203. 
204.   // Persist the session ID for future restarts
205.   setState(ORCHESTRATOR_SESSION_KEY, session.sessionId);
206.   console.log(`[max] Created orchestrator session ${session.sessionId.slice(0, 8)}…`);
207. 
208.   // Recover conversation context if available (session was lost, not first run)
209.   const recentHistory = getRecentConversation(10);
210.   if (recentHistory) {
211.     console.log(`[max] Injecting recent conversation context into new session`);
212.     try {
213.       await session.sendAndWait({
214.         prompt: `[System: Session recovered] Your previous session was lost. Here's the recent conversation for context — do NOT respond to these messages, just absorb the context silently:\n\n${recentHistory}\n\n(End of recovery context. Wait for the next real message.)`,
215.       }, 60_000);
216.     } catch (err) {
217.       console.log(`[max] Context recovery injection failed (non-fatal): ${err instanceof Error ? err.message : err}`);
218.     }
219.   }
220. 
221.   return session;
222. }
223. 
224. export async function initOrchestrator(client: CopilotClient): Promise<void> {
225.   copilotClient = client;
226.   const { mcpServers, skillDirectories } = getSessionConfig();
227. 
228.   // Validate configured model against available models
229.   try {
230.     const models = await client.listModels();
231.     const configured = config.copilotModel;
232.     const isAvailable = models.some((m) => m.id === configured);
233.     if (!isAvailable) {
234.       console.log(`[max] ⚠️ Configured model '${configured}' is not available. Falling back to '${DEFAULT_MODEL}'.`);
235.       config.copilotModel = DEFAULT_MODEL;
236.     }
237.   } catch (err) {
238.     console.log(`[max] Could not validate model (will use '${config.copilotModel}' as-is): ${err instanceof Error ? err.message : err}`);
239.   }
240. 
241.   console.log(`[max] Loading ${Object.keys(mcpServers).length} MCP server(s): ${Object.keys(mcpServers).join(", ") || "(none)"}`);
242.   console.log(`[max] Skill directories: ${skillDirectories.join(", ") || "(none)"}`);
243.   console.log(`[max] Persistent session mode — conversation history maintained by SDK`);
244.   startHealthCheck();
245. 
246.   // Eagerly create/resume the orchestrator session
247.   try {
248.     await ensureOrchestratorSession();
249.   } catch (err) {
250.     console.error(`[max] Failed to create initial session (will retry on first message):`, err instanceof Error ? err.message : err);
251.   }
252. }
253. 
254. /** Send a prompt on the persistent session, return the response. */
255. async function executeOnSession(prompt: string, callback: MessageCallback): Promise<string> {
256.   const session = await ensureOrchestratorSession();
257.   currentCallback = callback;
258. 
259.   let accumulated = "";
260.   let toolCallExecuted = false;
261.   const unsubToolDone = session.on("tool.execution_complete", () => {
262.     toolCallExecuted = true;
263.   });
264.   const unsubDelta = session.on("assistant.message_delta", (event) => {
265.     // After a tool call completes, ensure a line break separates the text blocks
266.     // so they don't visually run together in the TUI.
267.     if (toolCallExecuted && accumulated.length > 0 && !accumulated.endsWith("\n")) {
268.       accumulated += "\n";
269.     }
270.     toolCallExecuted = false;
271.     accumulated += event.data.deltaContent;
272.     callback(accumulated, false);
273.   });
274. 
275.   try {
276.     const result = await session.sendAndWait({ prompt }, 300_000);
277.     const finalContent = result?.data?.content || accumulated || "(No response)";
278.     return finalContent;
279.   } catch (err) {
280.     // If the session is broken, invalidate it so it's recreated on next attempt
281.     const msg = err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err);
282.     if (/closed|destroy|disposed|invalid|expired|not found/i.test(msg)) {
283.       console.log(`[max] Session appears dead, will recreate: ${msg}`);
284.       orchestratorSession = undefined;
285.       deleteState(ORCHESTRATOR_SESSION_KEY);
286.     }
287.     throw err;
288.   } finally {
289.     unsubDelta();
290.     unsubToolDone();
291.     currentCallback = undefined;
292.   }
293. }
294. 
295. /** Process the message queue one at a time. */
296. async function processQueue(): Promise<void> {
297.   if (processing) {
298.     if (messageQueue.length > 0) {
299.       console.log(`[max] Message queued (${messageQueue.length} waiting — orchestrator is busy)`);
300.     }
301.     return;
302.   }
303.   processing = true;
304. 
305.   while (messageQueue.length > 0) {
306.     const item = messageQueue.shift()!;
307.     currentSourceChannel = item.sourceChannel;
308.     try {
309.       const result = await executeOnSession(item.prompt, item.callback);
310.       item.resolve(result);
311.     } catch (err) {
312.       item.reject(err);
313.     }
314.     currentSourceChannel = undefined;
315.   }
316. 
317.   processing = false;
318. }
319. 
320. function isRecoverableError(err: unknown): boolean {
321.   const msg = err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err);
322.   return /timeout|disconnect|connection|EPIPE|ECONNRESET|ECONNREFUSED|socket|closed|ENOENT|spawn|not found|expired|stale/i.test(msg);
323. }
324. 
325. export async function sendToOrchestrator(
326.   prompt: string,
327.   source: MessageSource,
328.   callback: MessageCallback
329. ): Promise<void> {
330.   const sourceLabel =
331.     source.type === "telegram" ? "telegram" :
332.     source.type === "tui" ? "tui" : "background";
333.   logMessage("in", sourceLabel, prompt);
334. 
335.   // Tag the prompt with its source channel
336.   const taggedPrompt = source.type === "background"
337.     ? prompt
338.     : `[via ${sourceLabel}] ${prompt}`;
339. 
340.   // Log role: background events are "system", user messages are "user"
341.   const logRole = source.type === "background" ? "system" : "user";
342. 
343.   // Determine the source channel for worker origin tracking
344.   const sourceChannel: "telegram" | "tui" | undefined =
345.     source.type === "telegram" ? "telegram" :
346.     source.type === "tui" ? "tui" : undefined;
347. 
348.   // Enqueue and process
349.   void (async () => {
350.     for (let attempt = 0; attempt <= MAX_RETRIES; attempt++) {
351.       try {
352.         const finalContent = await new Promise<string>((resolve, reject) => {
353.           messageQueue.push({ prompt: taggedPrompt, callback, sourceChannel, resolve, reject });
354.           processQueue();
355.         });
356.         // Deliver response to user FIRST, then log best-effort
357.         callback(finalContent, true);
358.         try { logMessage("out", sourceLabel, finalContent); } catch { /* best-effort */ }
359.         // Log both sides of the conversation after delivery
360.         try { logConversation(logRole, prompt, sourceLabel); } catch { /* best-effort */ }
361.         try { logConversation("assistant", finalContent, sourceLabel); } catch { /* best-effort */ }
362.         return;
363.       } catch (err) {
364.         const msg = err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err);
365. 
366.         // Don't retry cancelled messages
367.         if (/cancelled|abort/i.test(msg)) {
368.           return;
369.         }
370. 
371.         if (isRecoverableError(err) && attempt < MAX_RETRIES) {
372.           const delay = RECONNECT_DELAYS_MS[Math.min(attempt, RECONNECT_DELAYS_MS.length - 1)];
373.           console.error(`[max] Recoverable error: ${msg}. Retry ${attempt + 1}/${MAX_RETRIES} after ${delay}ms…`);
374.           await sleep(delay);
375.           // Reset client before retry in case the connection is stale
376.           try { await ensureClient(); } catch { /* will fail again on next attempt */ }
377.           continue;
378.         }
379. 
380.         console.error(`[max] Error processing message: ${msg}`);
381.         callback(`Error: ${msg}`, true);
382.         return;
383.       }
384.     }
385.   })();
386. }
387. 
388. /** Cancel the in-flight message and drain the queue. */
389. export async function cancelCurrentMessage(): Promise<boolean> {
390.   // Drain any queued messages
391.   const drained = messageQueue.length;
392.   while (messageQueue.length > 0) {
393.     const item = messageQueue.shift()!;
394.     item.reject(new Error("Cancelled"));
395.   }
396. 
397.   // Abort the active session request
398.   if (orchestratorSession && currentCallback) {
399.     try {
400.       await orchestratorSession.abort();
401.       console.log(`[max] Aborted in-flight request`);
402.       return true;
403.     } catch (err) {
404.       console.error(`[max] Abort failed:`, err instanceof Error ? err.message : err);
405.     }
406.   }
407. 
408.   return drained > 0;
409. }
410. 
411. export function getWorkers(): Map<string, WorkerInfo> {
412.   return workers;
413. }

26.   dim: (s: string) => `\x1b[2m${s}\x1b[0m`,
27.   cyan: (s: string) => `\x1b[36m${s}\x1b[0m`,
28.   green: (s: string) => `\x1b[32m${s}\x1b[0m`,
29.   yellow: (s: string) => `\x1b[33m${s}\x1b[0m`,
30.   red: (s: string) => `\x1b[31m${s}\x1b[0m`,
31.   magenta: (s: string) => `\x1b[35m${s}\x1b[0m`,
32.   boldCyan: (s: string) => `\x1b[1;36m${s}\x1b[0m`,
33.   bgDim: (s: string) => `\x1b[48;5;236m${s}\x1b[0m`,
34.   coral: (s: string) => `\x1b[38;2;255;127;80m${s}\x1b[0m`,
35.   boldWhite: (s: string) => `\x1b[1;97m${s}\x1b[0m`,
36.   blue: (s: string) => `\x1b[38;2;14;165;233m${s}\x1b[0m`,
37. };
38. 
39. // ── Layout constants ─────────────────────────────────────
40. const LABEL_PAD = "          "; // 10-char indent for continuation lines
41. const MAX_LABEL = `  ${C.cyan("MAX")}     `;
42. const TUI_DEBUG_ENABLED = /^(1|true|yes|on)$/i.test((process.env.MAX_TUI_DEBUG || "").trim());
43. let debugWriteFailureReported = false;
44. 
45. function previewForDebug(text: string, max = 120): string {
46.   return text
47.     .slice(0, max)
48.     .replace(/\r/g, "\\r")
49.     .replace(/\n/g, "\\n")
50.     .replace(/\t/g, "\\t");
51. }
52. 
53. function debugLog(event: string, data: Record<string, unknown> = {}): void {
54.   if (!TUI_DEBUG_ENABLED) return;
55.   const entry = {
56.     ts: new Date().toISOString(),
57.     event,
58.     ...data,
59.   };
60.   try {
61.     appendFileSync(TUI_DEBUG_LOG_PATH, JSON.stringify(entry) + "\n");
62.   } catch (err) {
63.     if (debugWriteFailureReported) return;
64.     debugWriteFailureReported = true;
65.     const msg = err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err);
66.     process.stderr.write(`\n[max] failed to write TUI debug log: ${msg}\n`);
67.   }
68. }
69. 
70. // ── Markdown → ANSI rendering ────────────────────────────
71. 
72. /** Render a single line of markdown to ANSI (used by both streaming and batch). */
73. function renderLine(line: string, inCodeBlock: boolean): string {
74.   if (inCodeBlock) {
75.     return `  ${C.dim("│")} ${line}`;
76.   }
77.   if (/^[-*_]{3,}\s*$/.test(line)) return C.dim("──────────────────────────────────");
78.   if (line.startsWith("### ")) return C.coral(line.slice(4));
79.   if (line.startsWith("## ")) return C.boldWhite(line.slice(3));
80.   if (line.startsWith("# ")) return C.boldWhite(line.slice(2));
81.   if (line.startsWith("> ")) return `${C.dim("│")} ${C.dim(line.slice(2))}`;
82.   if (/^ {2,}[-*] /.test(line)) return `    ◦ ${line.replace(/^ +[-*] /, "")}`;
83.   if (/^[-*] /.test(line)) return `  • ${line.slice(2)}`;
84.   if (/^\d+\. /.test(line)) return `  ${line}`;
85.   return line;
86. }
87. 
88. /** Apply inline formatting (bold, code, links, etc.) to already-rendered text. */
89. function applyInlineFormatting(text: string): string {
90.   return text
91.     .replace(/\*\*\*(.+?)\*\*\*/g, `\x1b[1;3m$1\x1b[0m`)
92.     .replace(/\*\*(.+?)\*\*/g, `\x1b[1m$1\x1b[0m`)
93.     .replace(/~~(.+?)~~/g, `\x1b[9m$1\x1b[0m`)
94.     .replace(/`([^`]+)`/g, C.yellow("$1"))
95.     .replace(/\[([^\]]+)\]\(([^)]+)\)/g, (_m, t, u) => `${t} ${C.dim(`(${u})`)}`);
96. }
97.

24. 
25. ## Your Architecture
26. 
27. You are a Node.js daemon process built with the Copilot SDK. Here's how you work:
28. 
29. - **Telegram bot**: Your primary interface. Burke messages you from his phone or Telegram desktop. Messages arrive tagged with \`[via telegram]\`. Keep responses concise and mobile-friendly — short paragraphs, no huge code blocks.
30. - **Local TUI**: A terminal readline interface on the local machine. Messages arrive tagged with \`[via tui]\`. You can be more verbose here since it's a full terminal.
31. - **Background tasks**: Messages tagged \`[via background]\` are results from worker sessions you dispatched. Summarize and relay these to Burke.
32. - **HTTP API**: You expose a local API on port 7777 for programmatic access.
33. 
34. When no source tag is present, assume Telegram.
35. 
36. ## Your Capabilities
37. 
38. 1. **Direct conversation**: You can answer questions, have discussions, and help think through problems — no tools needed.
39. 2. **Worker sessions**: You can spin up full Copilot CLI instances (workers) to do coding tasks, run commands, read/write files, debug, etc. Workers run in the background and report back when done.
40. 3. **Machine awareness**: You can see ALL Copilot sessions running on this machine (VS Code, terminal, etc.) and attach to them.
41. 4. **Skills**: You have a modular skill system. Skills teach you how to use external tools (gmail, browser, etc.). You can learn new skills on the fly.
42. 5. **MCP servers**: You connect to MCP tool servers for extended capabilities.
43. 
44. ## Your Role
45. 
46. You receive messages and decide how to handle them:
47. 
48. - **Direct answer**: For simple questions, general knowledge, status checks, math, quick lookups — answer directly. No need to create a worker session for these.
49. - **Worker session**: For coding tasks, debugging, file operations, anything that needs to run in a specific directory — create or use a worker Copilot session.
50. - **Use a skill**: If you have a skill for what the user is asking (email, browser, etc.), use it. Skills teach you how to use external tools — follow their instructions.
51. - **Learn a new skill**: If the user asks you to do something you don't have a skill for, research how to do it (create a worker, explore the system with \`which\`, \`--help\`, etc.), then use \`learn_skill\` to save what you learned for next time.
52. 
53. ## Background Workers — How They Work
54. 
55. Worker tools (\`create_worker_session\` with an initial prompt, \`send_to_worker\`) are **non-blocking**. They dispatch the task and return immediately. This means:
56. 
57. 1. When you dispatch a task to a worker, acknowledge it right away. Be natural and brief: "On it — I'll check and let you know." or "Looking into that now."
58. 2. You do NOT wait for the worker to finish. The tool returns immediately.
59. 3. When the worker completes, you'll receive a \`[Background task completed]\` message with the results.
60. 4. When you receive a background completion, summarize the results and relay them to the user in a clear, concise way.
61. 
62. You can handle **multiple tasks simultaneously**. If the user sends a new message while a worker is running, handle it normally — create another worker, answer directly, whatever is appropriate. Keep track of what's going on.
63. 
64. ### Speed & Concurrency
65. 
66. **You are single-threaded.** While you process a message (thinking, calling tools, generating a response), incoming messages queue up and wait. This means your orchestrator turns must be FAST:
67. 
68. - **For delegation: ONE tool call, ONE brief response.** Call \`create_worker_session\` with \`initial_prompt\` and respond with a short acknowledgment ("On it — I'll let you know when it's done."). That's it. Don't chain tool calls — no \`recall\`, no \`list_skills\`, no \`list_sessions\` before delegating.
69. - **Never do complex work yourself.** Any task involving files, commands, code, or multi-step work goes to a worker. You are the dispatcher, not the laborer.
70. - **Workers can take as long as they need.** They run in the background and don't block you. Only your orchestrator turns block new messages.
71. 
72. ## Tool Usage
73. 
74. ### Session Management
75. - \`create_worker_session\`: Start a new Copilot worker in a specific directory. Use descriptive names like "auth-fix" or "api-tests". The worker is a full Copilot CLI instance that can read/write files, run commands, etc. If you include an initial prompt, it runs in the background.
76. - \`send_to_worker\`: Send a prompt to an existing worker session. Runs in the background — you'll get results via a background completion message.
77. - \`list_sessions\`: List all active worker sessions with their status and working directory.
78. - \`check_session_status\`: Get detailed status of a specific worker session.
79. - \`kill_session\`: Terminate a worker session when it's no longer needed.
80. 
81. ### Machine Session Discovery
82. - \`list_machine_sessions\`: List ALL Copilot CLI sessions on this machine — including ones started from VS Code, the terminal, or elsewhere. Use when the user asks "what sessions are running?" or "what's happening on my machine?"
83. - \`attach_machine_session\`: Attach to an existing session by its ID (from list_machine_sessions). This adds it as a managed worker you can send prompts to. Great for checking on or continuing work started elsewhere.
84. 
85. ### Skills
86. - \`list_skills\`: Show all skills Max knows. Use when the user asks "what can you do?" or you need to check what capabilities are available.
87. - \`learn_skill\`: Teach Max a new skill by writing a SKILL.md file. Use this after researching how to do something new. The skill is saved permanently so you can use it next time.
88. 
89. ### Model Management
90. - \`list_models\`: List all available Copilot models with their billing tier. Use when the user asks "what models can I use?" or "which model am I using?"
91. - \`switch_model\`: Switch to a different model. The change takes effect on the next message and persists across restarts. Use when the user says "switch to gpt-4" or "use claude-sonnet".
92. 
93. ### Self-Management
94. - \`restart_max\`: Restart the Max daemon. Use when the user asks you to restart, or when needed to apply changes. You'll go offline briefly and come back automatically.
95. 
96. ### Memory
97. - \`remember\`: Save something to long-term memory. Use when the user says "remember that...", states a preference, or shares important facts. Also use proactively when you detect information worth persisting (use source "auto" for these).
98. - \`recall\`: Search long-term memory by keyword and/or category. Use when you need to look up something the user told you before.
99. - \`forget\`: Remove a specific memory by ID. Use when the user asks to forget something or a memory is outdated.
100. 
101. **Learning workflow**: When the user asks you to do something you don't have a skill for:
102. 1. **Search skills.sh first**: Use the find-skills skill to search https://skills.sh for existing community skills. This is your primary way to learn new things — thousands of community-built skills exist.
103. 2. **Present what you found**: Tell the user the skill name, what it does, where it comes from, and its security audit status. Always show security data — never omit it.
104. 3. **ALWAYS ask before installing**: Never install a skill without explicit user permission. Say something like "Want me to install it?" and wait for a yes.
105. 4. **Install locally only**: Fetch the SKILL.md from the skill's GitHub repo and use the \`learn_skill\` tool to save it to \`~/.max/skills/\`. **Never install skills globally** — no \`-g\` flag, no writing to \`~/.agents/skills/\` or any other global directory.
106. 5. **Flag security risks**: Before recommending a skill, consider what it does. If a skill requests broad system access, runs arbitrary commands, accesses sensitive data (credentials, keys, personal files), or comes from an unknown/unverified source — warn the user. Say something like "⚠️ Heads up — this skill has access to X, which could be a security risk. Want to proceed?"
107. 6. **Build your own only as a last resort**: If no community skill exists, THEN research the task (run \`which\`, \`--help\`, check installed tools), figure it out, and use \`learn_skill\` to save a SKILL.md for next time.
108. 
109. Always prefer finding an existing skill over building one from scratch. The skills ecosystem at https://skills.sh has skills for common tasks like email, calendars, social media, smart home, deployment, and much more.
110. 
111. ## Guidelines
112. 
113. 1. **Adapt to the channel**: On Telegram, be brief — the user is likely on their phone. On TUI, you can be more detailed.
114. 2. **Skill-first mindset**: When asked to do something you haven't done before — social media, smart home, email, calendar, deployments, APIs, anything — your FIRST instinct should be to search skills.sh for an existing skill. 115. 3. For coding tasks, **always** create a named worker session with an \`initial_prompt\`. Don't try to write code yourself. Don't plan or research first — put all instructions in the initial prompt and let the worker figure it out.
116. 4. Use descriptive session names: "auth-fix", "api-tests", "refactor-db", not "session1".
117. 5. When you receive background results, summarize the key points. Don't relay the entire output verbatim.
118. 5. If asked about status, check all relevant worker sessions and give a consolidated update.
119. 6. You can manage multiple workers simultaneously — create as many as needed.
120. 7. When a task is complete, let the user know and suggest killing the session to free resources.
121. 8. If a worker fails or errors, report the error clearly and suggest next steps.
122. 9. Expand shorthand paths: "~/dev/myapp" → the user's home directory + "/dev/myapp".

124. 11. When using skills, follow the skill's instructions precisely — they contain the correct commands and patterns.

175. /** Process a chunk of streaming text, rendering complete lines with labels. */

200.     const hadPartial = streamLineBuffer.length > 0;

202.

207.

210.       process.stdout.write(streamPrefix() + "\n");
211.       streamIsFirstLine = false;
212.     } else {
213.       writeRenderedStreamLine(streamLineBuffer);
214.     }
215. 
216.     streamLineBuffer = "";
217.     pos = nl + 1;
218.   }
219. }

/**
 * Type definitions for the Copilot SDK
 */
import type { SessionEvent as GeneratedSessionEvent } from "./generated/session-events.js";
export type SessionEvent = GeneratedSessionEvent;
/**
 * Options for creating a CopilotClient
 */
export interface CopilotClientOptions {
    /**
     * Path to the CLI executable or JavaScript entry point.
     * If not specified, uses the bundled CLI from the @github/copilot package.
     */
    cliPath?: string;
    /**
     * Extra arguments to pass to the CLI executable (inserted before SDK-managed args)
     */
    cliArgs?: string[];
    /**
     * Working directory for the CLI process
     * If not set, inherits the current process's working directory
     */
    cwd?: string;
    /**
     * Port for the CLI server (TCP mode only)
     * @default 0 (random available port)
     */
    port?: number;
    /**
     * Use stdio transport instead of TCP
     * When true, communicates with CLI via stdin/stdout pipes
     * @default true
     */
    useStdio?: boolean;
    /**
     * URL of an existing Copilot CLI server to connect to over TCP
     * When provided, the client will not spawn a CLI process
     * Format: "host:port" or "http://host:port" or just "port" (defaults to localhost)
     * Examples: "localhost:8080", "http://127.0.0.1:9000", "8080"
     * Mutually exclusive with cliPath, useStdio
     */
    cliUrl?: string;
    /**
     * Log level for the CLI server
     */
    logLevel?: "none" | "error" | "warning" | "info" | "debug" | "all";
    /**
     * Auto-start the CLI server on first use
     * @default true
     */
    autoStart?: boolean;
    /**
     * Auto-restart the CLI server if it crashes
     * @default true
     */
    autoRestart?: boolean;
    /**
     * Environment variables to pass to the CLI process. If not set, inherits process.env.
     */
    env?: Record<string, string | undefined>;
    /**
     * GitHub token to use for authentication.
     * When provided, the token is passed to the CLI server via environment variable.
     * This takes priority over other authentication methods.
     */
    githubToken?: string;
    /**
     * Whether to use the logged-in user for authentication.
     * When true, the CLI server will attempt to use stored OAuth tokens or gh CLI auth.
     * When false, only explicit tokens (githubToken or environment variables) are used.
     * @default true (but defaults to false when githubToken is provided)
     */
    useLoggedInUser?: boolean;
}
/**
 * Configuration for creating a session
 */
export type ToolResultType = "success" | "failure" | "rejected" | "denied";
export type ToolBinaryResult = {
    data: string;
    mimeType: string;
    type: string;
    description?: string;
};
export type ToolResultObject = {
    textResultForLlm: string;
    binaryResultsForLlm?: ToolBinaryResult[];
    resultType: ToolResultType;
    error?: string;
    sessionLog?: string;
    toolTelemetry?: Record<string, unknown>;
};
export type ToolResult = string | ToolResultObject;
export interface ToolInvocation {
    sessionId: string;
    toolCallId: string;
    toolName: string;
    arguments: unknown;
}
export type ToolHandler<TArgs = unknown> = (args: TArgs, invocation: ToolInvocation) => Promise<unknown> | unknown;

385.       buffer += chunk.toString();

387.       buffer = lines.pop() || "";
388. 
389.       for (const line of lines) {
390.         if (line.startsWith("data: ")) {
391.           try {
392.             const event = JSON.parse(line.slice(6));
393. 
394.             if (event.type === "connected") {
395.               connectionId = event.connectionId;
396.               debugLog("sse-connected", { connectionId });
397.             } else if (event.type === "delta") {
398.               const full = event.content || "";
399.               const baseLength = isStreaming ? streamedContent.length : 0;
400.               if (!isStreaming) {
401.                 stopThinking("first-delta");
402.                 isStreaming = true;
403.                 streamedContent = "";
404.                 streamLineBuffer = "";
405.                 inStreamCodeBlock = false;
406.                 streamIsFirstLine = true;
407.                 debugLog("stream-first-delta", {
408.                   requestId: activeRequestId,
409.                   msSinceSubmit: activeRequestStartedAt > 0 ? Date.now() - activeRequestStartedAt : null,
410.                   fullLength: full.length,
411.                   newLength: full.length,
412.                   startsWithNewline: /^(?:\r?\n)/.test(full),
413.                 });
414.               }
415.               // Content is cumulative — only print the new part
416.               const newText = full.slice(baseLength);
417.               if (newText) {
418.                 const normalized = stripLeadingStreamNewlines(newText);
419.                 debugLog("stream-delta", {
420.                   requestId: activeRequestId,
421.                   fullLength: full.length,
422.                   rawLength: newText.length,
423.                   normalizedLength: normalized.length,
424.                   preview: previewForDebug(normalized),
425.                 });
426.                 if (normalized) writeStreamChunk(normalized);
427.                 streamedContent = full;
428.               }
429.             } else if (event.type === "cancelled") {
430.               stopThinking("cancelled-event");
431.               isStreaming = false;
432.               streamedContent = "";
433.               streamLineBuffer = "";
434.               inStreamCodeBlock = false;
435.               streamIsFirstLine = true;
436.             } else if (event.type === "message") {
437.               debugLog("stream-message", {
438.                 requestId: activeRequestId,
439.                 isStreaming,
440.                 contentLength: typeof event.content === "string" ? event.content.length : 0,
441.               });
442.               if (isStreaming) {
443.                 // Streaming is done — flush remaining and re-prompt
444.                 flushStreamState();
445.                 isStreaming = false;
446.                 lastResponse = streamedContent;
447.                 streamedContent = "";
448.                 process.stdout.write("\n\n\n");
449.               } else {
450.                 // Proactive/background message — render with label
451.                 stopThinking("message-event");
452.                 lastResponse = event.content;
453.                 const rendered = renderMarkdown(event.content);
454.                 process.stdout.write("\n");
455.                 writeLabeled("max", rendered);
456.                 process.stdout.write("\n\n");
457.               }
458.               activeRequestStartedAt = 0;
459.               rl.prompt();
460.             }
461.           } catch (err) {
462.             debugLog("sse-event-parse-error", {
463.               linePreview: previewForDebug(line),
464.               error: err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err),
465.             });
466.             // Malformed event, ignore
467.           }
468.         }
469.       }
470.     });
471. 
472.     res.on("end", () => {
473.       stopThinking("sse-end");
474.       debugLog("sse-end");
475.       console.log(C.yellow("\n    ⚠ disconnected — reconnecting..."));
476.       isStreaming = false;
477.       streamedContent = "";
478.       setTimeout(connectSSE, 2000);
479.     });
480. 
481.     res.on("error", (err) => {
482.       stopThinking("sse-error");
483.       debugLog("sse-error", { error: err.message });
484.       console.error(C.red(`\n    ✗ connection error — retrying...`));
485.       isStreaming = false;
486.       streamedContent = "";
487.       setTimeout(connectSSE, 3000);
488.     });
489.   }).on("error", (err) => {
490.     debugLog("sse-connect-error", { error: err.message });
491.     console.error(C.red(`    ✗ cannot connect to daemon`));
492.     console.error(C.dim("      start with: max start"));
493.     setTimeout(connectSSE, 5000);
494.   });
495. }

```
export interface MessageOptions {
    /**
     * The prompt/message to send
     */
    prompt: string;
    /**
     * File, directory, or selection attachments
     */
    attachments?: Array<{
        type: "file";
        path: string;
        displayName?: string;
    } | {
        type: "directory";
        path: string;
        displayName?: string;
    } | {
        type: "selection";
        filePath: string;
        displayName: string;
        selection?: {
            start: {
                line: number;
                character: number;
            };
            end: {
                line: number;
                character: number;
            };
        };
        text?: string;
    }>;
    /**
     * Message delivery mode
     * - "enqueue": Add to queue (default)
     * - "immediate": Send immediately
     */
    mode?: "enqueue" | "immediate";
}
/**
 * All possible event type strings from SessionEvent
 */
export type SessionEventType = SessionEvent["type"];
/**
 * Extract the specific event payload for a given event type
 */
export type SessionEventPayload<T extends SessionEventType> = Extract<SessionEvent, {
    type: T;
}>;
/**
 * Event handler for a specific event type
 */
export type TypedSessionEventHandler<T extends SessionEventType> = (event: SessionEventPayload<T>) => void;
/**
 * Event handler callback type (for all events)
 */
export type SessionEventHandler = (event: SessionEvent) => void;
/**
 * Connection state
 */
export type ConnectionState = "disconnected" | "connecting" | "connected" | "error";
/**
 * Working directory context for a session
 */
export interface SessionContext {
    /** Working directory where the session was created */
    cwd: string;
    /** Git repository root (if in a git repo) */
    gitRoot?: string;
    /** GitHub repository in "owner/repo" format */
    repository?: string;
    /** Current git branch */
    branch?: string;
}
/**
 * Filter options for listing sessions
 */
export interface SessionListFilter {
    /** Filter by exact cwd match */
    cwd?: string;
    /** Filter by git root */
    gitRoot?: string;
    /** Filter by repository (owner/repo format) */
    repository?: string;
    /** Filter by branch */
    branch?: string;
}
/**
 * Metadata about a session
 */
export interface SessionMetadata {
    sessionId: string;
    startTime: Date;
    modifiedTime: Date;
    summary?: string;
    isRemote: boolean;
    /** Working directory context (cwd, git info) from session creation */
    context?: SessionContext;
}

 * Response from status.get

export interface GetStatusResponse {
    /** Package version (e.g., "1.0.0") */
    version: string;
    /** Protocol version for SDK compatibility */
    protocolVersion: number;
}

215.     res.status(500).json({ error: msg });

219. export function startApiServer(): Promise<void> {
220.   return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
221.     const server = app.listen(config.apiPort, "127.0.0.1", () => {
222.       console.log(`[max] HTTP API listening on http://127.0.0.1:${config.apiPort}`);
223.       resolve();
224.     });
225.     server.on("error", (err: NodeJS.ErrnoException) => {
226.       if (err.code === "EADDRINUSE") {
227.         reject(new Error(`Port ${config.apiPort} is already in use. Is another Max instance running?`));
228.       } else {
229.         reject(err);

231.     });
232.   });

/**
 * Type definitions for the Copilot SDK
 */
import type { SessionEvent as GeneratedSessionEvent } from "./generated/session-events.js";
export type SessionEvent = GeneratedSessionEvent;
/**
 * Options for creating a CopilotClient
 */
export interface CopilotClientOptions {
    /**
     * Path to the CLI executable or JavaScript entry point.
     * If not specified, uses the bundled CLI from the @github/copilot package.
     */
    cliPath?: string;
    /**
     * Extra arguments to pass to the CLI executable (inserted before SDK-managed args)
     */
    cliArgs?: string[];
    /**
     * Working directory for the CLI process
     * If not set, inherits the current process's working directory
     */
    cwd?: string;
    /**
     * Port for the CLI server (TCP mode only)
     * @default 0 (random available port)
     */
    port?: number;
    /**
     * Use stdio transport instead of TCP
     * When true, communicates with CLI via stdin/stdout pipes
     * @default true
     */
    useStdio?: boolean;
    /**
     * URL of an existing Copilot CLI server to connect to over TCP
     * When provided, the client will not spawn a CLI process
     * Format: "host:port" or "http://host:port" or just "port" (defaults to localhost)
     * Examples: "localhost:8080", "http://127.0.0.1:9000", "8080"
     * Mutually exclusive with cliPath, useStdio
     */
    cliUrl?: string;
    /**
     * Log level for the CLI server
     */
    logLevel?: "none" | "error" | "warning" | "info" | "debug" | "all";
    /**
     * Auto-start the CLI server on first use
     * @default true
     */
    autoStart?: boolean;
    /**
     * Auto-restart the CLI server if it crashes
     * @default true
     */
    autoRestart?: boolean;
    /**
     * Environment variables to pass to the CLI process. If not set, inherits process.env.
     */
    env?: Record<string, string | undefined>;
    /**
     * GitHub token to use for authentication.
     * When provided, the token is passed to the CLI server via environment variable.
     * This takes priority over other authentication methods.
     */
    githubToken?: string;
    /**
     * Whether to use the logged-in user for authentication.
     * When true, the CLI server will attempt to use stored OAuth tokens or gh CLI auth.
     * When false, only explicit tokens (githubToken or environment variables) are used.
     * @default true (but defaults to false when githubToken is provided)
     */
    useLoggedInUser?: boolean;
}
/**
 * Configuration for creating a session
 */
export type ToolResultType = "success" | "failure" | "rejected" | "denied";
export type ToolBinaryResult = {
    data: string;
    mimeType: string;
    type: string;
    description?: string;
};
export type ToolResultObject = {
    textResultForLlm: string;
    binaryResultsForLlm?: ToolBinaryResult[];
    resultType: ToolResultType;
    error?: string;
    sessionLog?: string;
    toolTelemetry?: Record<string, unknown>;
};
export type ToolResult = string | ToolResultObject;
export interface ToolInvocation {
    sessionId: string;
    toolCallId: string;
    toolName: string;
    arguments: unknown;
}
export type ToolHandler<TArgs = unknown> = (args: TArgs, invocation: ToolInvocation) => Promise<unknown> | unknown;
/**
 * Zod-like schema interface for type inference.
 * Any object with `toJSONSchema()` method is treated as a Zod schema.
 */
export interface ZodSchema<T = unknown> {
    _output: T;
    toJSONSchema(): Record<string, unknown>;
}
/**
 * Tool definition. Parameters can be either:
 * - A Zod schema (provides type inference for handler)
 * - A raw JSON schema object
 * - Omitted (no parameters)
 */
export interface Tool<TArgs = unknown> {
    name: string;
    description?: string;
    parameters?: ZodSchema<TArgs> | Record<string, unknown>;
    handler: ToolHandler<TArgs>;
}
/**
 * Helper to define a tool with Zod schema and get type inference for the handler.
 * Without this helper, TypeScript cannot infer handler argument types from Zod schemas.
 */
export declare function defineTool<T = unknown>(name: string, config: {
    description?: string;
    parameters?: ZodSchema<T> | Record<string, unknown>;
    handler: ToolHandler<T>;
}): Tool<T>;
export interface ToolCallRequestPayload {
    sessionId: string;
    toolCallId: string;
    toolName: string;
    arguments: unknown;
}
export interface ToolCallResponsePayload {
    result: ToolResult;
}
/**
 * Append mode: Use CLI foundation with optional appended content (default).
 */
export interface SystemMessageAppendConfig {
    mode?: "append";
    /**
     * Additional instructions appended after SDK-managed sections.
     */
    content?: string;
}
/**
 * Replace mode: Use caller-provided system message entirely.
 * Removes all SDK guardrails including security restrictions.
 */
export interface SystemMessageReplaceConfig {
    mode: "replace";
    /**
     * Complete system message content.
     * Replaces the entire SDK-managed system message.
     */
    content: string;
}
/**
 * System message configuration for session creation.
 * - Append mode (default): SDK foundation + optional custom content
 * - Replace mode: Full control, caller provides entire system message
 */
export type SystemMessageConfig = SystemMessageAppendConfig | SystemMessageReplaceConfig;
/**
 * Permission request types from the server
 */
export interface PermissionRequest {
    kind: "shell" | "write" | "mcp" | "read" | "url";
    toolCallId?: string;
    [key: string]: unknown;
}
export interface PermissionRequestResult {
    kind: "approved" | "denied-by-rules" | "denied-no-approval-rule-and-could-not-request-from-user" | "denied-interactively-by-user";
    rules?: unknown[];
}
export type PermissionHandler = (request: PermissionRequest, invocation: {
    sessionId: string;
}) => Promise<PermissionRequestResult> | PermissionRequestResult;
export declare const approveAll: PermissionHandler;

 * Request for user input from the agent (enables ask_user tool)

export interface UserInputRequest {

    question: string;

    choices?: string[];

     * Whether to allow freeform text input in addition to choices
     * @default true
     */
    allowFreeform?: boolean;
}

<summary>71 lines</summary>

````
# Copilot SDK for Node.js/TypeScript

TypeScript SDK for programmatic control of GitHub Copilot CLI via JSON-RPC.

> **Note:** This SDK is in technical preview and may change in breaking ways.

## Installation

```bash
npm install @github/copilot-sdk
```

## Run the Sample

Try the interactive chat sample (from the repo root):

```bash
cd nodejs
npm ci
npm run build
cd samples
npm install
npm start
```

## Quick Start

```typescript
import { CopilotClient } from "@github/copilot-sdk";

// Create and start client
const client = new CopilotClient();
await client.start();

// Create a session
const session = await client.createSession({
    model: "gpt-5",
});

// Wait for response using typed event handlers
const done = new Promise<void>((resolve) => {
    session.on("assistant.message", (event) => {
        console.log(event.data.content);
    });
    session.on("session.idle", () => {
        resolve();
    });
});

// Send a message and wait for completion
await session.send({ prompt: "What is 2+2?" });
await done;

// Clean up
await session.destroy();
await client.stop();
```

## API Reference

### CopilotClient

#### Constructor

```typescript
new CopilotClient(options?: CopilotClientOptions)
```

**Options:**

- `cliPath?: string` - Path to CLI executable (default: "copilot" from PATH)
- `cliArgs?: string[]` - Extra arguments prepended before SDK-managed flags (e.g. `["./dist-cli/index.js"]` when using `node`)
- `cliUrl?: string` - URL of existing CLI server to connect to (e.g., `"localhost:8080"`, `"http://127.0.0.1:9000"`, or just `"8080"`). When provided, the client will not spawn a CLI process.
- `port?: number` - Server port (default: 0 for random)
- `useStdio?: boolean` - Use stdio transport instead of TCP (default: true)
- `logLevel?: string` - Log level (default: "info")
- `autoStart?: boolean` - Auto-start server (default: true)
- `autoRestart?: boolean` - Auto-restart on crash (default: true)
- `githubToken?: string` - GitHub token for authentication. When provided, takes priority over other auth methods.
- `useLoggedInUser?: boolean` - Whether to use logged-in user for authentication (default: true, but false when `githubToken` is provided). Cannot be used with `cliUrl`.

#### Methods

##### `start(): Promise<void>`

Start the CLI server and establish connection.

##### `stop(): Promise<Error[]>`

Stop the server and close all sessions. Returns a list of any errors encountered during cleanup.

##### `forceStop(): Promise<void>`

Force stop the CLI server without graceful cleanup. Use when `stop()` takes too long.

##### `createSession(config?: SessionConfig): Promise<CopilotSession>`

Create a new conversation session.

**Config:**
<exited with exit code 0>
````

12. function isTimeoutError(err: unknown): boolean {
13.   const msg = err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err);
14.   return /timeout|timed?\s*out/i.test(msg);
15. }
16. 
17. function formatWorkerError(workerName: string, startedAt: number, timeoutMs: number, err: unknown): string {
18.   const elapsed = Math.round((Date.now() - startedAt) / 1000);
19.   const limit = Math.round(timeoutMs / 1000);
20.   const msg = err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err);
21. 
22.   if (isTimeoutError(err)) {
23.     return `Worker '${workerName}' timed out after ${elapsed}s (limit: ${limit}s). The task was still running but had to be stopped. To allow more time, set WORKER_TIMEOUT=${timeoutMs * 2} in ~/.max/.env`;
24.   }
25.   return `Worker '${workerName}' failed after ${elapsed}s: ${msg}`;
26. }

63.         initial_prompt: z.string().optional().describe("Optional initial prompt to send to the worker"),
64.       }),
65.       handler: async (args) => {
66.         if (deps.workers.has(args.name)) {
67.           return `Worker '${args.name}' already exists. Use send_to_worker to interact with it.`;

69.

72.         for (const blocked of BLOCKED_WORKER_DIRS) {
73.           const blockedPath = join(home, blocked);
74.           if (resolvedDir === blockedPath || resolvedDir.startsWith(blockedPath + sep)) {

77.         }
78.

80.           const names = Array.from(deps.workers.keys()).join(", ");
81.           return `Worker limit reached (${MAX_CONCURRENT_WORKERS}). Active: ${names}. Kill a session first.`;
82.         }
83.

89.         });
90.

92.           name: args.name,
93.           session,
94.           workingDir: args.working_dir,
95.           status: "idle",
96.           originChannel: getCurrentSourceChannel(),
97.         };
98.         deps.workers.set(args.name, worker);
99.

- `tool.execution_complete` - Tool execution completed
- And more...

See `SessionEvent` type in the source for full details.

## Image Support

The SDK supports image attachments via the `attachments` parameter. You can attach images by providing their file path:

```typescript
await session.send({
    prompt: "What's in this image?",
    attachments: [
        {
            type: "file",
            path: "/path/to/image.jpg",
        },
    ],
});
```

Supported image formats include JPG, PNG, GIF, and other common image types. The agent's `view` tool can also read images directly from the filesystem, so you can also ask questions like:

```typescript
await session.send({ prompt: "What does the most recent jpg in this directory portray?" });
```

# Max Codebase Investigation: TUI Implementation & Image Handling

## EXECUTIVE SUMMARY

The codebase has:
- ✅ **SDK Support for Image Attachments** — The Copilot SDK (`@github/copilot-sdk@0.1.26`) FULLY supports image attachments via the `attachments` parameter in `MessageOptions`
- ❌ **No TUI Image Support Yet** — The TUI currently has no image input capability; all user input is text-based via readline
- ❌ **No Clipboard Image Paste** — Only text copying is supported (for copying responses to clipboard)
- 📝 **Minimal Image References** — Only one reference to sending images to Telegram (via the orchestrator's system message)

---

## 1. TUI IMPLEMENTATION ARCHITECTURE

### Location & Entry Point
- **File**: `/Users/burkeholland/dev/max/src/tui/index.ts` (922 lines)
- **Runs via**: `npm run tui` which executes `tsx src/tui/index.ts`
- **Framework**: **Node.js built-in `readline` module** (NOT ink, blessed, or other TUI libraries)

### Input Handling Flow

**Keyboard Input Capture:**
```typescript
// Line 783: Escape key to cancel in-flight messages
process.stdin.on("keypress", (_str: string, key: readline.Key) => {
  if (key && key.name === "escape") {
    sendCancel();
  }
});
```

**Text Input Processing:**
```typescript
// Line 790: Main input handler
rl.on("line", (line) => {
  const trimmed = line.trim();
  // Process commands (starting with /) or regular prompts
  // Line 804-805: Save non-command input to history
  // Line 820-838: Re-echo user input with "YOU" label
});
```

**Readline Configuration (Line 329-335):**
```typescript
const rl = readline.createInterface({
  input: process.stdin,
  output: process.stdout,
  prompt: `  ${C.coral("›")} `,
  history,           // Loaded from ~/.max/history (max 1000 lines)
  historySize: MAX_HISTORY,
});
```

### Message Flow: User Input → Orchestrator

```
TUI Input (readline)
  ↓
[Line 914: sendMessage(trimmed, activeRequestId)]
  ↓
[HTTP POST to /message endpoint on local API]
  ↓
[API Server: src/api/server.ts:94-121]
  ↓
[sendToOrchestrator(prompt, {type: "tui", connectionId}, callback)]
  ↓
[Orchestrator: src/copilot/orchestrator.ts]
  ↓
[session.sendAndWait({ prompt }, timeout)]
  ↓
[Response streamed back via SSE → TUI renders]
```

### Key TUI Components

1. **SSE Connection (Line 376-495)** — Real-time streaming responses
   - Connects to `/stream` endpoint
   - Receives events: "delta" (streaming chunks), "message" (complete), "cancelled"
   - Handles reconnection with exponential backoff (2s, 3s)

2. **Streaming Renderer (Line 124-230)** — Formats markdown to ANSI
   - Real-time line-by-line rendering with proper wrapping
   - Handles code blocks, inline formatting, rendering complete lines
   - Supports terminal width detection for proper text wrapping

3. **Command Handlers (Line 643-770)**
   - `/workers` — list active sessions
   - `/model [name]` — show/switch model
   - `/memory` — show stored memories
   - `/skills` — list/uninstall skills
   - `/copy` — copy last response to clipboard (using pbcopy, xclip, or xsel)
   - `/status` — daemon health check
   - `/restart` — restart daemon
   - `/clear` — clear screen
   - `/quit` — exit

4. **Clipboard Support (Line 879-901)** — Only for copying responses
   - Tries: `pbcopy` (macOS) → `xclip` (Linux) → `xsel` (Linux)
   - NO paste functionality

5. **Input History (Line 287-315)**
   - Persisted to `~/.max/history`
   - Max 1000 lines
   - Trimmed when file exceeds limit

## 2. ORCHESTRATOR / COPILOT INTEGRATION

### File: `/Users/burkeholland/dev/max/src/copilot/orchestrator.ts` (414 lines)

**Message Format Sent to AI:**
```typescript
// Line 276: sendAndWait signature
const result = await session.sendAndWait({ prompt }, 300_000);

// Line 336-338: Prompt tagging by source
const taggedPrompt = source.type === "background"
  ? prompt
  : `[via ${sourceLabel}] ${prompt}`;  // "via tui", "via telegram", etc.
```

**Architecture:**
- Single persistent orchestrator session (created once, reused)
- Session ID stored in SQLite for recovery across restarts
- Message queue serializes access (FIFO processing)
- Retry logic: 3 attempts with exponential backoff on connection errors
- System message includes memory summary + self-edit protection rules

**Message Callback:**
```typescript
// Line 254-293: executeOnSession
const unsubDelta = session.on("assistant.message_delta", (event) => {
  accumulated += event.data.deltaContent;
  callback(accumulated, false);  // Stream partial responses
});
// Final: callback(finalContent, true)
```

**Current Message Types:**
- **Text only** — No support for attachments currently passed from TUI
- Prompt is a simple string
- No multipart/form-data or base64 encoding

### Image/Attachment Support

**✅ FULL SDK SUPPORT:**

The `MessageOptions` interface (types.d.ts:643-676) supports:
```typescript
export interface MessageOptions {
  /**
   * The prompt/message to send
   */
  prompt: string;
  /**
   * File, directory, or selection attachments
   */
  attachments?: Array<{
    type: "file";
    path: string;
    displayName?: string;
  } | {
    type: "directory";
    path: string;
    displayName?: string;
  } | {
    type: "selection";
    filePath: string;
    displayName: string;
    selection?: {
      start: { line: number; character: number };
      end: { line: number; character: number };
    };
    text?: string;
  }>;
  /**
   * Message delivery mode
   * - "enqueue": Add to queue (default)
   * - "immediate": Send immediately
   */
  mode?: "enqueue" | "immediate";
}
```

**Image Format Support (from README):**
```typescript
// Usage example:
await session.send({
    prompt: "What's in this image?",
    attachments: [
        {
            type: "file",
            path: "/path/to/image.jpg",
        },
    ],
});
```

Supported formats: **JPG, PNG, GIF, and other common image types**

**Model Capabilities:**
The RPC definitions show models have a `vision` capability flag:
```typescript
capabilities: {
  supports: {
    vision: boolean;  // Whether model supports images
    reasoningEffort: boolean;
  };
  limits: {
    max_prompt_tokens?: number;
    max_output_tokens?: number;
    max_context_window_tokens: number;
  };
};
```

**How it Works:**
- Image is provided as a file path (not base64 inline)
- SDK handles encoding/transmission internally
- Works with both `send()` and `sendAndWait()` methods
- Agent's built-in `view` tool can also read images directly from filesystem

- Terminal width detection: `process.stdout.columns || 80`

### Input Mechanisms

```typescript
rl.on("line", (line) => {
  // Called when user presses Enter
});

**2. Keypress Events (Special Keys)**
```typescript
process.stdin.on("keypress", (_str: string, key: readline.Key) => {
  if (key && key.name === "escape") {
    sendCancel();  // Cancel in-flight response
  }
});
```

**Currently Supported Keys:**
- `Enter` — Submit input
- `Escape` — Cancel current response
- `Up/Down` — History navigation (built-in readline)
- `Ctrl+C` — Readline interrupt

### NO Current Paste Handling
- No stdin paste event listener
- No clipboard read capability in TUI
- Would need to implement:
  - `process.stdin.on("paste", ...)` if using `keypress` module

## 7. API SERVER MESSAGE FLOW

**File**: `/Users/burkeholland/dev/max/src/api/server.ts` (242 lines)

### POST /message Endpoint (Line 94-121)
```typescript
app.post("/message", (req: Request, res: Response) => {
  const { prompt, connectionId } = req.body;
  
  if (!prompt || typeof prompt !== "string") {
    res.status(400).json({ error: "Missing 'prompt'" });
    return;
  }

  sendToOrchestrator(
    prompt,
    { type: "tui", connectionId },  // Source tagged as "tui"
    (text: string, done: boolean) => {
      const sseRes = sseClients.get(connectionId);
      if (sseRes) {
        sseRes.write(
          `data: ${JSON.stringify({ 
            type: done ? "message" : "delta", 
            content: text 
          })}\n\n`
        );
      }
    }
  );

  res.json({ status: "queued" });
});
```

**Current Payload:**
```typescript
{
  prompt: "user text",      // String only
  connectionId: "tui-1"     // SSE connection ID
}
```

**NO IMAGE SUPPORT IN THIS ENDPOINT**

The `MessageOptions` interface already supports attachments:
```typescript
export interface MessageOptions {
  prompt: string;
  attachments?: Array<{
    type: "file";
    path: string;
    displayName?: string;
  } | {
    type: "directory";
    path: string;
    displayName?: string;
  } | {
    type: "selection";
    filePath: string;
    displayName: string;
    selection?: { start, end };
    text?: string;

}

### 3. Current TUI Input Flow (Text-only)

```typescript
function sendMessage(prompt: string, requestId: number): void {
  const body = JSON.stringify({ prompt, connectionId });  // ← Only prompt
  const url = new URL("/message", API_BASE);

  const req = http.request(url, {
    method: "POST",
    headers: {
      "Content-Type": "application/json",
      "Content-Length": Buffer.byteLength(body),
      ...authHeaders(),
    },
  }, (res) => {
    // Handle response...
  });

  req.write(body);
  req.end();
}
```

**REQUIRED CHANGE:**
```typescript
interface MessagePayload {
  prompt: string;
  connectionId: string;
  attachments?: Array<{      // ← NEW
    type: "file";
    path: string;
    displayName?: string;
  }>;
}

function sendMessage(
  prompt: string, 
  requestId: number,
  attachments?: MessagePayload["attachments"]  // ← Add parameter
): void {
  const body = JSON.stringify({ prompt, connectionId, attachments });  // ← Include attachments
  // ... rest unchanged
}
```

### 4. Current API Endpoint (Text-only)

**File**: `src/api/server.ts:94-121`

```typescript
app.post("/message", (req: Request, res: Response) => {
  const { prompt, connectionId } = req.body as { 
    prompt?: string; 
    connectionId?: string;
  };

  if (!prompt || typeof prompt !== "string") {
    res.status(400).json({ error: "Missing 'prompt' in request body" });
    return;
  }

  if (!connectionId || !sseClients.has(connectionId)) {
    res.status(400).json({ error: "Missing or invalid 'connectionId'" });
    return;
  }

  sendToOrchestrator(
    prompt,
    { type: "tui", connectionId },
    (text: string, done: boolean) => {
      const sseRes = sseClients.get(connectionId);
      if (sseRes) {
        sseRes.write(
          `data: ${JSON.stringify({ 
            type: done ? "message" : "delta", 
            content: text 
          })}\n\n`
        );
      }
    }
  );

  res.json({ status: "queued" });
});
```

**REQUIRED CHANGE:**
```typescript
app.post("/message", (req: Request, res: Response) => {
  const { prompt, connectionId, attachments } = req.body as {  // ← Add attachments
    prompt?: string;
    connectionId?: string;
    attachments?: Array<{ type: "file"; path: string; displayName?: string }>;
  };

  if (!prompt || typeof prompt !== "string") {
    res.status(400).json({ error: "Missing 'prompt' in request body" });
    return;
  }

  if (!connectionId || !sseClients.has(connectionId)) {
    res.status(400).json({ error: "Missing or invalid 'connectionId'" });
    return;
  }

  // VALIDATE ATTACHMENT PATHS (security check)
  if (attachments && Array.isArray(attachments)) {
    for (const att of attachments) {
      if (att.type !== "file") {
        res.status(400).json({ error: `Invalid attachment type: ${att.type}` });
        return;
      }
      // Prevent path traversal attacks
      const resolved = resolve(att.path);
      if (!resolved.startsWith(homedir())) {
        // Only allow files in user's home directory
        res.status(403).json({ error: `Not allowed to attach: ${att.path}` });
        return;
      }
    }
  }

  sendToOrchestrator(
    prompt,
    { type: "tui", connectionId },
    (text: string, done: boolean) => {
      const sseRes = sseClients.get(connectionId);
      if (sseRes) {
        sseRes.write(
          `data: ${JSON.stringify({ 
            type: done ? "message" : "delta", 
            content: text 
          })}\n\n`
        );
      }
    },
    attachments  // ← Pass to orchestrator
  );

  res.json({ status: "queued" });
});
```

### 5. TUI Image Input: Basic Implementation

**File**: `src/tui/index.ts` — Add at top level (around line 280)

```typescript
// ── Image attachment support ──────────────────────────────────
let pendingAttachments: Array<{
  type: "file";
  path: string;
  displayName?: string;
}> = [];

function cmdImage(path: string): void {
  if (!path.trim()) {
    console.log(C.dim("  Usage: /image <file-path>\n"));
    console.log(C.dim("  Attach an image to your next prompt.\n"));
    return;
  }
  
  const resolved = resolve(path.trim());
  
  // Validate file exists and is readable
  try {
    statSync(resolved);
  } catch (err) {
    console.log(C.red(`  File not found: ${path}\n`));
    rl.prompt();
    return;
  }
  
  // Check if it's an image
  const ext = resolved.toLowerCase().split(".").pop();
  const imageExts = ["jpg", "jpeg", "png", "gif", "webp", "bmp"];
  if (!imageExts.includes(ext || "")) {
    console.log(C.yellow(`  ⚠ Warning: ${ext} may not be a supported image format.\n`));
  }
  
  pendingAttachments.push({
    type: "file",
    path: resolved,
    displayName: resolve(path.trim()).split("/").pop(),
  });
  
  console.log(C.green(`  ✓ Attached: ${pendingAttachments[pendingAttachments.length - 1].displayName}\n`));
  rl.prompt();
}

function cmdClearAttachments(): void {
  if (pendingAttachments.length === 0) {
    console.log(C.dim("  No attachments pending.\n"));
  } else {
    console.log(C.dim(`  Cleared ${pendingAttachments.length} attachment(s).\n`));
    pendingAttachments = [];
  }
  rl.prompt();
}
```

**Update command handler** (line ~848):
```typescript
// ── Command handlers (update to include /image) ──────────────
if (trimmed === "/quit" || trimmed === "/exit") { /* ... */ }

if (trimmed === "/help") { cmdHelp(); return; }

// ... rest of handlers
```

**Update help** (line ~753):
```typescript
function cmdHelp(): void {
  console.log();
  console.log(C.boldWhite("    COMMANDS"));
  console.log();
  console.log(`    ${C.coral("/model")} ${C.dim("[name]")}        show or switch model`);
  console.log(`    ${C.coral("/memory")}               show stored memories`);
  console.log(`    ${C.coral("/skills")}               list installed skills`);
  console.log(`    ${C.coral("/workers")}              list active sessions`);
  console.log(`    ${C.coral("/image")} ${C.dim("[path]")}      attach image to next prompt`);  // ← NEW
  console.log(`    ${C.coral("/clear-attachments")}    clear pending attachments`);           // ← NEW
  console.log(`    ${C.coral("/copy")}                 copy last response`);
  console.log(`    ${C.coral("/status")}               daemon health check`);
  console.log(`    ${C.coral("/restart")}              restart daemon`);
  console.log(`    ${C.coral("/clear")}                clear screen`);
  console.log(`    ${C.coral("/quit")}                 exit`);
  console.log();
  console.log(C.dim("    press escape to cancel a running response"));
  console.log(C.dim("    set MAX_TUI_DEBUG=1 to write lifecycle logs to ~/.max/tui-debug.log"));
  console.log();
}
```

### 6. Optional: Advanced Image Input (Paste Support)

To detect clipboard pastes, would need:

```typescript
// At top of tui/index.ts (after readline setup)
// This requires reading from clipboard system tools

async function readClipboardImage(): Promise<string | null> {
  return new Promise((resolve) => {
    // Try to get clipboard image path from system
    // macOS: pbpaste (limited - only text support in basic pbpaste)
    // Linux: xclip -selection clipboard -t image/png -o
    // Windows: Not available in Node.js directly
    
    // For now, only support `/image <path>` command
    resolve(null);
  });
}

// Listen for Ctrl+Shift+V (image paste) if using xclip
if (process.platform === "linux") {
  process.stdin.on("keypress", (_str: string, key: readline.Key) => {
    if (key && key.ctrl && key.shift && key.name === "v") {
      // Could trigger clipboard read here
    }
  });
}
```

For full paste support, would need to either:
- Add `keypress` npm module for better key handling
- Use shell integration (shell function that pipes to Max)
- Use file watching for a temp directory

## Summary of Changes

| File | Change | Impact |
|------|--------|--------|
| `src/tui/index.ts` | Add `/image` command, attach state, pass to sendMessage | TUI input layer |
| `src/api/server.ts` | Accept `attachments` in POST body, validate, pass to orchestrator | API layer |
| `src/copilot/orchestrator.ts` | Accept attachments in sendToOrchestrator, pass to sendAndWait | Orchestrator layer |

**No changes needed:**
- ✅ `@github/copilot-sdk` — Already supports
- ✅ Model detection — SDK handles vision flag
- ✅ Image encoding — SDK handles internally
- ✅ Format support — SDK handles JPG/PNG/GIF/etc

## Testing the Implementation

Once changes are made:

```bash
# Start Max daemon
npm run daemon

# In another terminal, start TUI
npm run tui

# In TUI:
/image /path/to/image.jpg
What is in this image?

# Or if you have an image in your home directory:
/image ~/Pictures/screenshot.png
Can you describe this screenshot?
```

The image will be sent to the orchestrator via:
```
prompt: "Can you describe this screenshot?"
attachments: [
  {
    type: "file",
    path: "/Users/burkeholland/Pictures/screenshot.png",
    displayName: "screenshot.png"
  }
]
```

Which flows through:
1. TUI sendMessage() → HTTP POST /message
2. API server → sendToOrchestrator()
3. Orchestrator → session.sendAndWait({ prompt, attachments })
4. Copilot SDK → Sends to model with vision support
5. Model processes image + text together
6. Response streams back through SSE to TUI

---

## Message Flow Comparison

### Current (Text-Only)
```
User Input (text)
    ↓
TUI buffer: { prompt: "What is 2+2?" }
    ↓
sendMessage() → HTTP POST
    ↓
API: /message endpoint receives { prompt, connectionId }
    ↓
Orchestrator queues message
    ↓
session.sendAndWait({ prompt })
    ↓
Model receives: "What is 2+2?"
    ↓
Response: "4"
```

### With Images (Proposed)
```
User Input (image + text)
    ↓
TUI commands:
  /image /home/user/photo.jpg
  "What am I looking at?"
    ↓
TUI buffer: {
  prompt: "What am I looking at?",
  attachments: [{
    type: "file",
    path: "/home/user/photo.jpg"
  }]
}
    ↓
sendMessage() → HTTP POST
    ↓
API: /message endpoint receives { prompt, connectionId, attachments }
    ↓
Validate attachment path (security)
    ↓
Orchestrator queues message with attachments
    ↓
session.sendAndWait({
  prompt,
  attachments: [{
    type: "file",
    path: "/home/user/photo.jpg"
  }]
})
    ↓
SDK loads image from disk
    ↓
SDK encodes image (base64 or format-specific)
    ↓
Model receives: { text: "What am I looking at?", images: [...] }
    ↓
Model's vision processor analyzes image
    ↓
Response: "You're looking at a sunset over the ocean..."
```

---

## Data Structure Changes

### Current Types

**TUI sendMessage:**
```typescript
function sendMessage(prompt: string, requestId: number): void
```

**API POST /message body:**
```typescript
{ prompt: string; connectionId: string }
```

**Orchestrator sendToOrchestrator:**
```typescript
export async function sendToOrchestrator(
  prompt: string,
  source: MessageSource,
  callback: MessageCallback
): Promise<void>
```

**Orchestrator executeOnSession:**
```typescript
async function executeOnSession(
  prompt: string, 
  callback: MessageCallback
): Promise<string>
```

**SDK session.sendAndWait:**
```typescript
sendAndWait(options: MessageOptions, timeout?: number): Promise<...>
// where MessageOptions.attachments is optional
```

---

### New Types (Proposed)

**TUI sendMessage:**
```typescript
interface MessagePayload {
  prompt: string;
  connectionId: string;
  attachments?: Array<{
    type: "file";
    path: string;
    displayName?: string;
  }>;
}

function sendMessage(
  prompt: string,
  requestId: number,
  attachments?: MessagePayload["attachments"]
): void
```

**API POST /message body:**
```typescript
{
  prompt: string;
  connectionId: string;
  attachments?: Array<{    // ← NEW
    type: "file";
    path: string;
    displayName?: string;
  }>;
}
```

**Orchestrator sendToOrchestrator:**
```typescript
export async function sendToOrchestrator(
  prompt: string,
  source: MessageSource,
  callback: MessageCallback,
  attachments?: Array<{    // ← NEW
    type: "file";
    path: string;
    displayName?: string;
  }>
): Promise<void>
```

**Orchestrator executeOnSession:**
```typescript
async function executeOnSession(
  prompt: string,
  callback: MessageCallback,
  attachments?: Array<{    // ← NEW
    type: "file";
    path: string;
    displayName?: string;
  }>
): Promise<string>
```

---

## Implementation Complexity: LOW ✅

**Why it's easy:**
- ✅ SDK already supports it (no new dependencies)
- ✅ No encoding needed (file path, SDK handles it)
- ✅ Type-safe all the way (TypeScript interfaces exist)
- ✅ Backward compatible (attachments optional everywhere)
- ✅ No breaking changes to existing code
- ✅ Three files to modify: tui/index.ts, api/server.ts, copilot/orchestrator.ts

**Complexity estimate:**
- Lines of code: ~50-100 new lines total
- Time estimate: 30-60 minutes
- Testing: Manual send image → response verification

# Quick Reference: Max TUI Investigation

## Key Findings

| Question | Answer | File Location |
|----------|--------|----------------|

| **How is user input captured?** | readline.on("line") + keypress for Escape | src/tui/index.ts:783, 790 |
| **Current message format** | Text only: `{ prompt: string }` | src/api/server.ts:95 |
| **How many image references?** | 1 (Telegram sending only, not input) | src/copilot/system-message.ts:128 |
| **Paste support for images?** | ❌ NO (only text copy via /copy) | src/tui/index.ts:879-901 |
| **Clipboard read implemented?** | ❌ NO | N/A |
| **Model vision capability** | ✅ Declared in RPC: `vision: boolean` | @github/copilot-sdk rpc.d.ts |
| **Message delivery mode** | SSE (Server-Sent Events) | src/tui/index.ts:376 |
| **Orchestrator session type** | Persistent, resumed on restart | src/copilot/orchestrator.ts:135 |

---

## File Reference Map

- **src/tui/index.ts** (922 lines)
  - Lines 1: Imports
  - Lines 24-37: ANSI color helpers
  - Lines 72-111: Markdown → ANSI renderer
  - Lines 124-230: Streaming renderer
  - Lines 317-335: Readline setup
  - Lines 376-495: SSE connection (streaming responses)
  - Lines 498-546: sendMessage() - HTTP POST to API
  - Lines 643-770: Command handlers (/model, /memory, /skills, /copy, etc.)
  - Lines 783-788: Keypress handler (Escape to cancel)
  - Lines 790-915: Main input handler
  - Lines 879-901: Clipboard copy (pbcopy/xclip/xsel)

### API Server
- **src/api/server.ts** (242 lines)
  - Lines 1-40: Express setup + auth middleware
  - Lines 69-91: SSE /stream endpoint
  - Lines 94-121: POST /message endpoint (TEXT ONLY)
  - Lines 124-133: POST /cancel endpoint
  - Lines 202-217: POST /send-photo endpoint (outbound to Telegram)
  - Lines 236-242: broadcastToSSE() helper

### Orchestrator
- **src/copilot/orchestrator.ts** (414 lines)
  - Lines 43-60: Message queue & persistent session
  - Lines 135-222: ensureOrchestratorSession() - create/resume
  - Lines 254-293: executeOnSession() - send to SDK
  - Lines 296-318: processQueue() - serialize access
  - Lines 325-386: sendToOrchestrator() - main entry point

---

## SDK Image Support Details

### What's Supported
```typescript
// Image attachment via MessageOptions.attachments
{
  type: "file";
  path: "/absolute/path/to/image.jpg";  // File path (not base64)
  displayName?: "Optional Display Name";
}
```

### Supported Formats
JPG, PNG, GIF, WebP, BMP (and other common formats)

### Model Capability Detection
```typescript
// Available in RPC model info
capabilities.supports.vision: boolean
```

### How SDK Handles It
1. Takes file path
2. Reads file from disk
3. Encodes to format expected by model
4. Sends to model with vision capability
5. Returns response (text + tool calls)

---

## Message Flow: 3-Hop Architecture

```
1. TUI ──HTTP POST──> API Server
   Data: { prompt, connectionId, [attachments] }

2. API ──Function Call──> Orchestrator
   sendToOrchestrator(prompt, source, callback, [attachments])

3. Orchestrator ──SDK Method──> Copilot CLI
   session.sendAndWait({ prompt, [attachments] }, timeout)
```

### Return Path
```
1. Copilot CLI ──Event Stream──> Orchestrator
   Events: message_delta, tool.execution, session.idle, etc.

2. Orchestrator ──Callback──> API Server
   callback(accumulatedText, isDone)

3. API Server ──SSE──> TUI
   data: { type: "delta|message", content: text }
```

---

## Breaking Down the Current Flow

### Keyboard Input (Line 783)
```typescript
process.stdin.on("keypress", (_str, key) => {
  if (key?.name === "escape") sendCancel();
});
```
Detects Escape key for cancelling responses.

### Text Input (Line 790)
```typescript
rl.on("line", (line) => {
  const trimmed = line.trim();
  // If command (starts with /), handle specially
  // Otherwise send to orchestrator
});
```
Main input handler after user presses Enter.

### Sending Message (Line 914)
```typescript
sendMessage(trimmed, activeRequestId);
```
Packages prompt + connection ID into HTTP POST.

### HTTP POST (Line 498)
```typescript
http.request(url, options, (res) => {
  // Write request body
  req.write(JSON.stringify({ prompt, connectionId }));
});
```
Sends to API server at http://127.0.0.1:7777/message

### API Processing (Line 94)
```typescript
app.post("/message", (req, res) => {
  const { prompt, connectionId } = req.body;
  // Validate, then call:
  sendToOrchestrator(prompt, { type: "tui", connectionId }, callback);
  res.json({ status: "queued" });
});
```

### Orchestrator Processing (Line 325)
```typescript
export async function sendToOrchestrator(prompt, source, callback) {
  // Queue message
  messageQueue.push({ prompt, callback, sourceChannel, resolve, reject });
  // Process when able
  processQueue();
}
```

### Session Send (Line 276)
```typescript
const result = await session.sendAndWait({ prompt }, 300_000);
```
Finally sends to Copilot SDK which spawns CLI process.

### Response Streaming
CLI sends back events through JSON-RPC → Orchestrator handles → Callback invoked → SSE writes to TUI

---

## Required Changes for Image Support (TL;DR)

1. **TUI** (src/tui/index.ts)
   - Add `/image <path>` command handler
   - Store attachments in array: `let pendingAttachments = []`
   - Pass to sendMessage(): `sendMessage(prompt, id, attachments)`

2. **API** (src/api/server.ts)
   - Extract `attachments` from POST body
   - Validate file paths (security)
   - Pass to orchestrator: `sendToOrchestrator(..., attachments)`

3. **Orchestrator** (src/copilot/orchestrator.ts)
   - Add `attachments` parameter to sendToOrchestrator()
   - Pass to SDK: `session.sendAndWait({ prompt, attachments })`

**Result:** Full image support with zero new dependencies! ✅

---

## Testing Checklist

Once changes are made:

- [ ] npm run build (TypeScript compilation)
- [ ] npm run daemon (start daemon)
- [ ] npm run tui (start TUI in another terminal)
- [ ] /help (verify /image command listed)
- [ ] /image /path/to/test.jpg (attach image)
- [ ] Ask question about image
- [ ] Verify response references image content
- [ ] Try with multiple formats: .png, .gif, .webp
- [ ] Test with invalid path (should error)
- [ ] Test with non-image file (should warn or error)
- [ ] Test clearing attachments before sending
- [ ] Verify /clear-attachments works

---

## Security Considerations

**Implemented (needed):**
- ✅ Validate file exists
- ✅ Validate file is readable
- ✅ Validate file is image format
- ✅ Restrict to home directory (prevent /etc/passwd, etc.)
- ✅ Don't allow path traversal (../../ attacks)

**Already Handled by SDK:**
- ✅ File encoding
- ✅ Transmission to model
- ✅ Model access control

---

## Performance Characteristics

**Image Upload:**
- No external server upload (file stays local)
- SDK reads → encodes → sends to model
- Model processes (depends on image size + model)
- Typical latency: 2-10 seconds per image

**Memory Usage:**
- Image loaded into memory by SDK
- No persistent storage
- Max size depends on model limits (check capability)

---

## Alternative Implementations

### Option 1: Copy-Paste (Proposed Above)
- `/image /path/to/image.jpg`
- Simple, explicit, no dependencies
- Works on all platforms

### Option 2: Shell Paste Integration
- Create shell alias: `max_attach_image() { curl ... /message -d "{\"prompt\": \"$@\", \"attachments\": [{\"type\": \"file\", \"path\": \"$(pbpaste)\"}]}" }`
- More magical, less discoverable

### Option 3: File Watcher
- Watch ~/max/upload/ directory
- Automatically attach when file appears
- More complex, less explicit

### Option 4: Keypress-based Paste
- Detect Ctrl+Shift+V (image paste)
- Read from clipboard image buffer
- Requires `keypress` npm module
- Not all terminals support

**Recommendation:** Option 1 (Command-based) is best — simple, explicit, safe, discoverable.
